  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447490240" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447490240?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=1001-books-to-read-before-you-die">1001-books-to-read-before-you-die</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447490240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13953105509378136608">Is there a way to escape the doom of society if you are not a rich, white, heterosexual, married man having "clean sex" with your own "lawful" wife with the purpose of producing a new generation of rich, white, heterosexual, married men? <br/><br/>Even the wife of this single category of human who is allowed shameless, guiltfree pleasure may not be free from shame and guilt. She may feel guilty for enjoying too much or too little what is expected of her as a marital duty. But at least she will have the sa</span>
  <span id="freeText13953105509378136608" style="display:none">Is there a way to escape the doom of society if you are not a rich, white, heterosexual, married man having "clean sex" with your own "lawful" wife with the purpose of producing a new generation of rich, white, heterosexual, married men? <br /><br />Even the wife of this single category of human who is allowed shameless, guiltfree pleasure may not be free from shame and guilt. She may feel guilty for enjoying too much or too little what is expected of her as a marital duty. But at least she will have the safety network of society to protect her when the nausea strikes. For all other human beings, not able to collect privileges like pearls on a string, not able to guide their desire towards conventional patriarchal rules, they are doomed to lose as soon as they enter the game.<br /><br />Giovanni knew and acted. David decided to block out knowledge and pretend there was nothing the matter. One died, the other lived. Both were doomed.<br /><br />Reading James Baldwin is like being infused with powerful sentences describing the abyss of patriarchy looming over individual lives. It is like going through the Purgatorio in Dante's Divina Commedia and ending up not in Heaven, but in Hell afterwards. The purity of life as imagined by the happy few who can actually "feel" according to the "moral" compass of patriarchy is hell on earth for all those who have to stay there without being able to live the part they act.<br /><br />What could have saved David and Giovanni? Unpoisoning their minds maybe, if that is possible?<br /><br />Taking away layer after layer of self-hatred and carefully implanted shame, until they'd be able to look at themselves in the mirror and see a happy, gay man and be proud? Is that entirely possible, even today? I don't know. I know it is not entirely possible for women, even in the most modern of societies, to break the rules of patriarchy without some loss of status, loss of respect, loss of financial security, loss of professional development. I imagine it would be the same for any person not enjoying the complete protection of privilege. For Giovanni it would never have been possible at the time and in the place where he moved. <br /><br />The only saving grace is that he found a storyteller to carry his voice beyond the finale.<br /><br />Love, love, love this short novel. Read it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13953105509378136608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1401355834?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iris" href="/user/show/17717848-iris">Iris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140184129" href="/book/show/828507.Giovanni_s_Room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17717848-iris?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17717848-iris?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17717848-iris?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401355834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15159652166501629709">I am in awe of James Baldwin's seamless way with words. His writing shakes me to my very core, I feel so vividly all the emotions described, the contradicting war within the world and within the self between hot, flaming fire and ice cold water, between fervent heat and stone cold detachment. The motif of water and the ocean and its metaphorical association with time, Giovanni's room itself, the inescapable self and claustrophobia particularly struck me- I feel overwhelmed and shaken by this tra</span>
  <span id="freeText15159652166501629709" style="display:none">I am in awe of James Baldwin's seamless way with words. His writing shakes me to my very core, I feel so vividly all the emotions described, the contradicting war within the world and within the self between hot, flaming fire and ice cold water, between fervent heat and stone cold detachment. The motif of water and the ocean and its metaphorical association with time, Giovanni's room itself, the inescapable self and claustrophobia particularly struck me- I feel overwhelmed and shaken by this tragic, beautiful, poignant and haunting novel. There is so much of literary and aesthetic worth to be explored in this book and also so much to be said about human psychology and consciousness, about the dangers of lying to oneself and hurting others, the dangers of self-hatred and lack of acceptance. I long to read another of Baldwin's books. I was completely captivated, drawn in and submerged by such seductive, visceral, melancholic prose- never have I felt such a tug at my emotions than the pull that was engendered in me and on my heart by this novel, though my life does not relate to the tale.</span>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781101907740" href="/book/show/25733998-giovanni-s-room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2537069292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4415762274188356810">I like this more than the three stars would indicate. The melodrama was a problem for me. The plot is simple and brilliantly done. David the American doesn’t want to admit he has homosexual impulses. His fiancée, Hella, doesn’t know he’s gay because David doesn’t know it. David is confused, as his friend Jacques at one point remarks. He’s experiencing major cognitive dissonance, simultaneously knowing something and acting as if it weren’t so. For he has met the beautiful, the irresistible Giovan</span>
  <span id="freeText4415762274188356810" style="display:none">I like this more than the three stars would indicate. The melodrama was a problem for me. The plot is simple and brilliantly done. David the American doesn’t want to admit he has homosexual impulses. His fiancée, Hella, doesn’t know he’s gay because David doesn’t know it. David is confused, as his friend Jacques at one point remarks. He’s experiencing major cognitive dissonance, simultaneously knowing something and acting as if it weren’t so. For he has met the beautiful, the irresistible Giovanni. Giovanni and David do it in the former’s squalid room, which David sees as a metaphor for punishment and grief, for poverty. There’s no goddamned way he’ll end up stuck in that rat hole. During their renovations, they remove bags of bricks from the room and scatter these in the neighborhood. (?) <br /><br />Now Hella is returning from Spain where she has gone briefly to think about whether she wants to marry David. David is set to dump Giovanni because he doesn’t want to be a faggot. No way, he wants to be a real American man, with the little woman putting the kids to bed at night while he’s in the study drinking himself to death and dreaming of cock. Soon his fiancée will learn the truth. Giovanni, driven mad by lost love, will be guillotined for a grisly crime. Yes, we’re in Paris. The writing style is assured, even mellifluous, if at times highly melodramatic in the manner of some—my least favorite—of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Emile%20Zola" title="Emile Zola" rel="nofollow noopener">Emile Zola</a>’s novels of social realism. The prose wavers between a kind of operatic hysteria and passages that are sonorous if not haunting. The <i>merde</i>’s about to hit the fan. Clear the room everyone. This <i>would</i> make a lovely opera. Is there a Rossini among us? Here’s your libretto.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2318619356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2318619356" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2318619356?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780141032948" href="/book/show/828503.Giovanni_s_Room">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">constricted hearts who live in fear</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=1001-before-you-die">1001-before-you-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2318619356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer753358960708492108"><b>
  <i>"You do, sometimes, remind me of the kind of man who is tempted to put himself in prison in order to avoid being hit by a car."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This insightful observation is made by Giovanni, to his lover David. An American in Paris, David is escaping from the conventional expectations he feels from his father, and pretty much everyone else in greater society. In Paris, he feels freer to live and love more honestly. But even in Paris, he and Giovanni are trapped in a shabby room with sightless windows, lest</span>
  <span id="freeText753358960708492108" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"You do, sometimes, remind me of the kind of man who is tempted to put himself in prison in order to avoid being hit by a car."</i>
</b><br /><br />This insightful observation is made by Giovanni, to his lover David. An American in Paris, David is escaping from the conventional expectations he feels from his father, and pretty much everyone else in greater society. In Paris, he feels freer to live and love more honestly. But even in Paris, he and Giovanni are trapped in a shabby room with sightless windows, lest anyone see them together. It is suffocating, dingy, and he longs desperately to get OUT of this room, away from his self-loathing, out where he can be 'normal'. Out, where his girlfriend Hella waits for him, with the potential for a traditional, acceptable life that has all the perfect shapes, and the appropriate pronouns. <br /><br />David doesn't realise that the suffocating closet he lives in has nothing whatsoever to do with Giovanni's room. His self-made prison goes with him like a shell on a turtle. It is always there, and is constructed completely from fear and repression. It is so much a part of David that it won't be removed. It will shield him from societal rejection, yes, but it also bars freedom, love, connection with another human, the ability for others to really know him.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"And no matter what I was doing, another me sat in my belly, absolutely cold with terror over the question of my life."</b>
</i><br /><br />This little novella is tight, packed with claustrophobic doom. It has an American-in-Europe charm to it reminiscent of Highsmith's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2247142.The_Talented_Mr__Ripley__Ripley___1_" title="The Talented Mr. Ripley (Ripley, #1) by Patricia Highsmith" rel="nofollow noopener">The Talented Mr. Ripley</a>. It's evident from the first page that James Baldwin is a beautiful writer, who wrote about things that he knew about, personally. He faced awful disadvantages being not only a black man in mid-20th-century, but a black, gay man. And how interesting that he decided to write a book featuring two gay, <i>white</i> characters. By doing that, he aptly demonstrates that being a gay guy in 1956 was a hell that even racial privilege couldn't avoid.<br /><br />There's some odd, (dare I say) misogynistic-y stuff floating around here, which is a bit disappointing. Lines like this: "Women are like water. They are tempting like that, and they can be that treacherous, and they can seem to be that bottomless, you know? - and they can be that shallow. And that dirty." I guess they <i>can</i> be, <i>anyone</i> can be tempting, treacherous, shallow and/or dirty. But women as a group? My disappointment was evened out somewhat by the character of Hella, who is intelligent, honest, and laments being dependent on a man. <br /> <br />This book addresses the specifics of living and loving out loud, using the example of being homosexual in an unaccepting world. But I think it translates well in a general way to all those who live secretively, whatever that secret may be. It speaks to those whose identity is so private, they feel painful isolation, to those whose fear has grown out of proportion, their need to conceal overshadowing the potential for happiness. This is the great tragedy at the heart of this book, and for those who live this reality. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>"...love him and let him love you. Do you think anything else under heaven really matters?"</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="753358960708492108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1167154096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1167154096" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565547225p2/11255849.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1167154096?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/11255849-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345806567" href="/book/show/17288631-giovanni-s-room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=vintage">vintage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=mesmerizing">mesmerizing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=french-oeuvre">french-oeuvre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=afro-american">afro-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=fav-authors">fav-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11255849-cheryl?shelf=the-psyche">the-psyche</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1167154096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11789116344696936255"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Then the door is before him. There is darkness all around him, there is silence in him. Then the door opens and he stands alone, the whole world falling away from him. And the brief corner of the sky seems to be shrieking, though he does not hear a sound. Then the earth tilts, he is thrown forward on his face in darkness, and his journey begins.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>Sometimes you read a book and you suddenly find yourself hijacked by a form of spellbinding intensity that spews from a participant narrator.</span>
  <span id="freeText11789116344696936255" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Then the door is before him. There is darkness all around him, there is silence in him. Then the door opens and he stands alone, the whole world falling away from him. And the brief corner of the sky seems to be shrieking, though he does not hear a sound. Then the earth tilts, he is thrown forward on his face in darkness, and his journey begins.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />Sometimes you read a book and you suddenly find yourself hijacked by a form of spellbinding intensity that spews from a participant narrator. You're pulled into the room, <i>Giovanni's Room,</i> and you soon find yourself emotionally involved with David's mental battle. You may not even like David, or like the way he treats people (his fiancee and his lover ), and yet, you're with him, rooting for him during his most piercing revelations. You even have sympathy for his dilemmas and meanders. But why is this? <br /><br />Blame Baldwin. Blame it on his hypnotic lyricism and pure poignancy that entraps the reader. Blame it on his story of self-conflict and melancholy, of reflection and remorse, of truth and lies and anything that embeds itself within the fabric of a life marred by deceit. Blame it on the forthrightness of a narrator whose words you follow intently:<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I remember that life in that room seemed to be occurring beneath the sea. Time flowed past indifferently above us; hours and days had no meaning. In the beginning, our life together held a joy and amazement which was newborn every day. Beneath the joy, of course, was anguish and beneath the amazement was fear; but they did not work themselves to the beginning until our high beginning was aloes on our tongues.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />The story starts in the present tense, with David (our narrator) reflecting on his life with Giovanni, his male lover. The story starts and you immediately sense that something has gone wrong, that you are at the cusp of what seems to be romantic tragedy, because David is embittered with remorse, regret and self-loathe: <i>"people are too various to be treated so lightly. I am too various to be trusted."</i> And then the story veers to the past tense, when David tells us the story from Giovanni's Room, a setting that was once the center of his life. He feels responsible for Giovanni's fate (as he narrates Giovanni is in prison), and he feels responsible for breaking his fiancee's(Hella) heart. <br /><br />David has come a long way, from New York to Paris, to avoid the conflict taking place within him. He is a gay man who wants to have a wife and a family. He is a gay man who wants to be accepted by society. He is a motherless gay son who wants to be accepted by his father:<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>A cavern opened in my mind, black, full of rumor, suggestion, of half-heard, half-forgotten, half-understood stories, full of dirty words. I thought I saw my future in that cavern. I was afraid. I could have cried, cried for shame and terror, cried for not understanding how this could have happened to me, how this could have happened in me.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />David's story of self-actualization is told in such a way that makes it relatable; to think of this vast world of ever-changing spectrum and to wonder wherein one can really find oneself. In this case, an American in Paris, a gay man in a conservative society, a young man figuring out his sexuality - the mistakes that accompany such awakenings. <br /><br />Reading this book, I was reminded of the sort of picture I yearned for in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5297.The_Picture_of_Dorian_Gray" title="The Picture of Dorian Gray by Oscar Wilde" rel="nofollow noopener">The Picture of Dorian Gray</a>, and while the setting, mood, and even some themes are reminiscent of <i>The American</i> by Henry James, what Baldwin does better is introduce characters only as they move the story forward, as a result, you see these characters more clearly. I can only imagine why this masterly written novel did not get more publicity, but the answer I come up with saddens me, for this is a transcendent piece of art that seems to be one of Baldwin's more poignant pieces.<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>When one begins to search for the crucial, the definitive moment, the moment which changed all others, one finds oneself pressing, in great pain, through a maze of false signals and abruptly locking doors.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11789116344696936255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_980410678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/980410678" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4643325-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535048395p2/4643325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980410678?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/4643325-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4643325-paul?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980410678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13184373513393674625">Often touted as a classic of gay literature, and I think quite rightly; this is a heartbreaking analysis of love, attachment and the struggle between what society expects and what is felt. Baldwin treats complex relationships with some warmth and no easy or comfortable answers. There is debate as to whether Baldwin is focussing on bisexuality, but you have to look at the context and the sense that the two main characters are on a journey of self discovery with varying degrees of acceptance.<br/>The t</span>
  <span id="freeText13184373513393674625" style="display:none">Often touted as a classic of gay literature, and I think quite rightly; this is a heartbreaking analysis of love, attachment and the struggle between what society expects and what is felt. Baldwin treats complex relationships with some warmth and no easy or comfortable answers. There is debate as to whether Baldwin is focussing on bisexuality, but you have to look at the context and the sense that the two main characters are on a journey of self discovery with varying degrees of acceptance.<br />The two main protagonists are David and Giovanni. David is an American currently living in Paris. He has a girlfriend, also an American, who is spending some time in Spain. David goes out for a drink with a gay acquaintance and meets Giovanni who is working in a bar. A passionate affair ensues, focussed on the room where Giovanni lives and where David spends much of his time. This idyllic, but doomed state of affairs continues until David’s girlfriend returns from Spain and decisions have to be made. Some of the novel is told in flashback and so the reader already knows the denouement; the point is the journey; the how. Considering this was written and set in the 1950s, it is a brave book with a clear battle between different value sets and a debate about what love is and isn’t. I wonder whether like Death in Venice we are looking at the Apollo/Dionysius split. Giovanni representing the passionate and unreasoning: David representing Apollo, more reserved, cerebral with the repression of emotion and denial of feeling. David feels like almost a detached observer of his own life. He has a very brief sexual relationship with a girl he meets, knowing it means more to her and knowing that for him it means very little. He detaches himself and is at a distance from his involvement and there is no care or concern for the needs, wants and feeling of the other. David does this with all those he relates to. He cannot accept his own self and this makes him very dangerous and damaging to others. To an extent, all the characters settle for what they don’t seem to be.<br />You could say that love doesn’t conquer all, but I’m not sure this is really about love at all; apart from Giovanni, who is destroyed by betrayal. It is about society’s expectations and about battles with identity and roles. A great novel creates debate, uncertainty and differing opinions and this is a great novel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13184373513393674625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1312788419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312788419" />
    <a title="Bianca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca"><img alt="Bianca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589154116p2/29843800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312788419?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bianca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bianca" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca">Bianca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=lgbtiq">lgbtiq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=us-author">us-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312788419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6567524465173323667">A few months ago, I was blown away by the documentary <i>I Am Not Your Negro</i>, which featured James Baldwin. I only heard of Baldwin a few years prior, via other GR friends' reviews of his books. I had his books on my TBR list, but they were there with six hundred other books ... <br/>Anyway, that documentary pushed me to seek some of his books. <br/><br/>It didn't occur to me when watching the documentary that Baldwin was gay. The poor man, being black and gay, during a very reprehensible period in US history. No</span>
  <span id="freeText6567524465173323667" style="display:none">A few months ago, I was blown away by the documentary <i>I Am Not Your Negro</i>, which featured James Baldwin. I only heard of Baldwin a few years prior, via other GR friends' reviews of his books. I had his books on my TBR list, but they were there with six hundred other books ... <br />Anyway, that documentary pushed me to seek some of his books. <br /><br />It didn't occur to me when watching the documentary that Baldwin was gay. The poor man, being black and gay, during a very reprehensible period in US history. Not only he had to fight against the white people, against the system because of his race, he had to hide and fight his own community's homophobia. No wonder he escaped to France for a while. <br /><br />Anyway, I had to remind myself that <i>Giovanni's Room</i> is not autobiographical, although it must have drawn inspiration from his personal experiences. I plan to read a bit more about Balwin and this novel.<br /><br />As I was reading <i>Giovanni's Room</i> I had to remind myself several times that the main character, David, an American in Paris, was a white man. David is in the closet and is ashamed by his one time encounter with a male friend. As the only child of a nice man, he feels it's his duty to be the "right" way. It's not only that, it's the 1950s and earlier, homosexuality is illegal. Paris though is more relaxed. While the cat was away, in this case, Hetta, David's fiancee, he has a dalliance with Giovanni, a beautiful and passionate Italian bartender, whom he met in a gay bar. The two have a passionate affair for a little while, even sharing Giovanni's small room. Giovanni's small, cluttered, dirty room is a metaphor of sorts for David's complex feelings, especially when he knows the time is approaching when he has to make a decision - to have a respectable life that includes a wife and kids or to give in to his preferences?<br /><br />It's important to remember that this was published in 1959. That's quite a feat in itself. The fact that it was written by a black man, way before the Civil movement, makes this novel even more significant.<br /><br />Baldwin's writing is beautifully lyrical and packaged tightly. You can sense the doubt and dread, the fear, the self-loathing. <br />None of the male characters is likeable, that includes David himself. <br /><br />This is a very sad novel, albeit one beautifully written.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6567524465173323667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_959998412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/959998412" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/959998412?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552077651" href="/book/show/828504.Giovanni_s_Room">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      Jeffrey Keeten
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=paris">paris</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=social-commentary">social-commentary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=1001-books">1001-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=sexuality">sexuality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer959998412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2744994927274619212">This is a tragedy of failed love in post-war Paris, featuring a protagonist as hard to judge as Camus' "The Stranger." The narrator, David, is a young man on an extended stay from the U.S. on parental funds, ostensibly to develop his writing skills, but in reality to play. A transient gay fling with an impoverished, artistic Bohemian leads to an idyllic cohabitation while his fiancé travels in the East. You know it didn’t last from the beginning of the book, but as the affair proceeds, you feel </span>
  <span id="freeText2744994927274619212" style="display:none">This is a tragedy of failed love in post-war Paris, featuring a protagonist as hard to judge as Camus' "The Stranger." The narrator, David, is a young man on an extended stay from the U.S. on parental funds, ostensibly to develop his writing skills, but in reality to play. A transient gay fling with an impoverished, artistic Bohemian leads to an idyllic cohabitation while his fiancé travels in the East. You know it didn’t last from the beginning of the book, but as the affair proceeds, you feel the delicious wonder of their love that is so liberating, you want it to last forever. Where so many travel tales open you to the adventure of exploring new worlds, this book sets the benchmark for a story of creating a world inside a room with the universe of two people. But then such a wrenching you are bound for. <br /><br />There is no focus on race in this tale, but the need for gays to "pass" as straight is revealed to be as much a corrupting a force as blacks considering passing as white not so long ago. And the phenomenon of internalized racism has its close parallel with the self’s importation of society’s disgust with same sex relations over much of history. I am always surprised when I learn of people who “discover” they are gay after long periods of living as straight. In this story I get some of such a reality when I learn how David has succeeded in erasing his early sexual experience with Joey at 13, a love discarded in a mental closet. <br /><br />First love is such a powerful theme in literature, but see if this little excerpt with Joey doesn’t get some special power and rank over other accounts from Baldwin’s skill and from the incident being so forbidden at the time:<br /><i>Joey raised his head as I lowered mine and we kissed, as it were by accident. Then, for the first time in my life, I was really aware of another person’s body, of another person’s smell. We had our arms around each other. It was like holding in my hand some rare, exhausted, nearly doomed bird which I ad miraculously happened to find. I was very frightened, I was sure he was frightened too, and we shut our eyes. To remember it so clearly, so painfully tonight tells me I never for an instant truly forgotten it. I feel in myself now a faint, dreadful stirring of what so overwhelmingly stirred in me then, great thirsty eat, and trembling, and tenderness so painful I thought my heart would burst. But out of this astounding, intolerable pain came joy, we have each other joy that night. It seemed, then, that a lifetime would not be long enough for me to act with Joey the act of love.</i><br /><br />And see if there isn’t something immortal here, something akin to the literary equivalent of a first climb of Everest:<br /><i>It was borne in on me: <u>But Joey is a boy.</u>. I saw suddenly the power in his thighs, in his arms, and in his loosely curled fists. The power and the promise and the mystery of that body made me suddenly afraid. The body suddenly seemed the black opening of a cavern in which I would be tortured till madness came, in which I would lose my manhood. Precisely, I wanted to know that mystery and feel that power and have that promise fulfilled through me. The sweat on my back grew cold. I grew ashamed. The very bed, in its sweet disorder, testified to vileness. I wondered what Joey’s mother would say when she saw the sheets. Then I thought of my father, who had no one in the world but me, my mother having died when I was little. A cavern opened in my mind, black, full of rumor, suggestion, of half-heard, half-forgotten, half-understood stories, full of dirty words. I thought I saw my future in that cavern. I was afraid. I could have cried, cried for shame and terror, cried for not understanding how this could have happened to me, how this could have happened <u>in</u> me.</i><br /><br />But all that is just background to the story here, but critical background. Once a person feels compelled to live a lie, some of one’s humanity inevitably gets eroded. The consequences of the moral choices and lies that David tells to Giovanni and to his future wife led me to some hateful responses, struggling all the while to find the forgiveness he was surely due. Much has changed since this was written, and much has not. There is still a frontier for anyone trying to chart the course of a bisexual identity, for, as explored recently in John Irving’s wonderful “In One Person”, they find themselves rejected or mistrusted by most gays and straights alike.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2744994927274619212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2025324299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025324299" />
    <a title="Paul Bryant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant"><img alt="Paul Bryant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1224113172p2/416390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025324299?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Bryant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Bryant" href="/user/show/416390-paul-bryant">Paul Bryant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780141032948" href="/book/show/828503.Giovanni_s_Room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/416390-paul-bryant?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025324299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8507795678807147764">In James Baldwin’s words:<br/><br/><i>They said I was a Negro writer and I would reach a very special audience. . . . And I would be dead if I alienated that audience. That, in effect, nobody would accept that book—coming from me. . . . My agent told me to burn it…. [the publishers] told me, ‘This new book will ruin your career, … and we won’t publish this book as a favor to you.’ </i><br/><br/>Fair enough, James Baldwin wanted to avoid being pigeonholed as a black writer. So made his protagonist here white. So here we ha</span>
  <span id="freeText8507795678807147764" style="display:none">In James Baldwin’s words:<br /><br /><i>They said I was a Negro writer and I would reach a very special audience. . . . And I would be dead if I alienated that audience. That, in effect, nobody would accept that book—coming from me. . . . My agent told me to burn it…. [the publishers] told me, ‘This new book will ruin your career, … and we won’t publish this book as a favor to you.’ </i><br /><br />Fair enough, James Baldwin wanted to avoid being pigeonholed as a black writer. So made his protagonist here white. So here we have a black writer presenting a gay love story about white people. And this book was published in the mid fifties. I mean, wow. That’s fearless. That’s reckless. <br /><br />If you look at the constellation of five star reviews and general critical opinion <i>Giovanni’s Room</i> is a resounding success. I can see why – this is a novel about a (white) American guy in Paris who’s proposed marriage to a woman who’s gone off for a few weeks to think about it (she has her issues too) and in the meantime he’s swept giddily into a love affair with a very handsome Italian waiter, with whom he ends up living, in the famous room, whilst horrifiedly waiting for The Fiancée to return, at which point he has to figure out what to do. Giovanni has wonderful pecs but can that justify a life of skulking and self-loathing and gradually turning into a porky middle aged fairy which is what, apparently, your fate is if you’re a gay man? <br /><br />Because according to our first person narrator, Americans are like this, French people are like that, men are like this, women are like that (he and his pals generalize like crazy), and gay men are either like <i>this</i> or like <i>that</i>, there’s nothing in between. So gay men are either middle aged, flabby wealthy fairies (his word) or “knife-thin” waiters and rent boys. One or the other. So many generalisations about so many people amidst this intense prose. Baldwin’s great control of place and atmosphere and melodramatic breathlessness pretty much successfully rushes you past all this dubious sexual politics which hardly any reviews mention. <br /><br />This book therefore gets like a million points for being a gay love story and exposing some gay men’s strong desire to stay in the closet and (I think) in the end saying that if you deny your own nature you’ll be left with less than nothing. But jeez, you could pull all kinds of quotes from here which gay-bashers would just love. It was really uncomfortable reading at times, for a whole number of reasons. <br /><br />Recommended : for Baldwin’s tremendous style and because this will really mess your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8507795678807147764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1879946296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1879946296" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1879946296?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345806567" href="/book/show/17288631-giovanni-s-room">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Edward by: </span>
      fortheloveofryan
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1879946296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8596397539469085584"><i>I'm disappointed. This book failed to deliver.<br/><br/>Buh-buh-but E.! You gave it five stars. <br/><br/>Shuddup, random person on the internet. You have no power here!<br/><br/>But how can you give it five stars if it failed?<br/><br/>Because it didn't make me gay.<br/><br/>Oh, okay. Wait... what?<br/><br/>It failed in making me gay. Homosexual, if you will. I do not, after having read this book, find men sexually attractive. Well, there is Johnny Depp. That's one pretty man. But, overall, I'm still, like, 99.9% straight. <br/><br/>What the fuck are you talking </i></span>
  <span id="freeText8596397539469085584" style="display:none"><i>I'm disappointed. This book failed to deliver.<br /><br />Buh-buh-but E.! You gave it five stars. <br /><br />Shuddup, random person on the internet. You have no power here!<br /><br />But how can you give it five stars if it failed?<br /><br />Because it didn't make me gay.<br /><br />Oh, okay. Wait... what?<br /><br />It failed in making me gay. Homosexual, if you will. I do not, after having read this book, find men sexually attractive. Well, there is Johnny Depp. That's one pretty man. But, overall, I'm still, like, 99.9% straight. <br /><br />What the fuck are you talking about?<br /><br />Even after having read this book, I cannot, for the life of me, choose to be gay. And who wouldn't want to be gay. Come on! But it's not working. I mean, I should be just jonesing for penis right now, right?<br /><br />That's... that's not how it works...<br /><br />Here, random person possibly growing more and more offended with every line of this false dialogue (psssst... it's actually just me talking to myself. I bet you're shocked. I know, right!), let me explain.</i><br /><br />Whiny bitches from a bygone age found this book disgusting and felt sure that it would spread the GAY AGENDA! Some felt that, just by reading this novel, you'd fall into a nest of vipers and partake in lurid booty sex with all the mens. Just reading this text could brainwash you into needing the D, especially if you, yourself, were in possession of some D. What was the general public to do? <br /><br />I keep hearing how whiny and triggered this new generation is today, but when you look back at the "good ol' days", you find that previous generations were scared of fucking EVERYTHING: gay people and women and commies and invisible men. Hell, some of these fools are still scared of all that. And Tom Cruise forbid your skin color is darker than Elmer's glue. How can old folks have been so terrified of such silly misconceptions but then turn around and call today's young people "too sensitive"? Get the fuck outta here, ya muppets.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room by James Baldwin" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a> is a terrific novel that follows an American in France. Our narrator's fiance has gone off to find herself and left him behind. He falls into a crowd of eccentrics, and ends up having a love affair with a man named Giovanni. The book is beautifully written. Some of the best, if not <i>the</i> best writing I've come across. Every word builds on the next, changing prose into music. Absolutely gorgeous. The level of word mastery on display here is awe inspiring. It will be a pleasure, I have no doubt, going through this author's back catalog. <br /><br />The only complaint I have are some ideas used that devalue women. Hella (the narrator's fiance) says at one point that all women are good for is getting pregnant and the narrator agrees. Giovanni and the narrator also have discussions on the uselessness of women. Didn't much care for that, but I couldn't tell if it was author intrusion or the character's personal beliefs. Because it wasn't obvious which, I'm not deducting any stars. <br /><br />Also, I call this guy "the narrator" because he's called both David and Butch in the book. Butch could've been a nickname, though, because only his father called him that. Unless I missed something. If that's the case, let me know in the comments. <br /><br />In summation: <i>Giovanni's Room</i> won't make you gay, but it will break your heart. If you love beautiful writing and touching stories, give it a try. My highest possible recommendation. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: More James Baldwin now, please.</b><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_178857215" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178857215" />
    <a title="Aubrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey"><img alt="Aubrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472535045p2/4119460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178857215?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aubrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aubrey" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey">Aubrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385334587" href="/book/show/527433.Giovanni_s_Room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=queer-as-in">queer-as-in</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=r-2014">r-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=prose-prose-prose">prose-prose-prose</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=1-read-on-hand">1-read-on-hand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=person-of-everything">person-of-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=shorty-short">shorty-short</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=antidote-think-twice-read">antidote-think-twice-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=r-goodreads">r-goodreads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178857215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2985217983134560366"><blockquote>
  <i>"If your countrymen think that privacy is a crime, so much the worse for your country..."</i>
</blockquote>Love is(n't) enough.<br/><br/>Love is(n't) enough in how it's done. Love is(n't) enough in how it's pressed upon and consolidated and ultimately allowed. When you look at it, especially when looking is all that's allowed, you start to feel that it's how it's always been, and you are the same as anyone. Unless you talk, which here on out is (never) the case. <br/><br/>But feeling, though. That's the compass of your crime. It</span>
  <span id="freeText2985217983134560366" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"If your countrymen think that privacy is a crime, so much the worse for your country..."</i>
</blockquote>Love is(n't) enough.<br /><br />Love is(n't) enough in how it's done. Love is(n't) enough in how it's pressed upon and consolidated and ultimately allowed. When you look at it, especially when looking is all that's allowed, you start to feel that it's how it's always been, and you are the same as anyone. Unless you talk, which here on out is (never) the case. <br /><br />But feeling, though. That's the compass of your crime. It breeds with the life and times and leaves you with nothing but a sense of righteousness and the basic plumbing. The birds and the bees, part A and part B, the diagrams of fitting and the hell of wondering otherwise. You can like the latter, you can drink it through you dry, but the founding fear will chase you across the ocean to where the rules are not as clear and just as cruel.<br /><br />But you are crueler. You're not the only one fumbling in the dark of man loves woman when each acts as so, you're not the only one realizing the gap between living and a life, you're not the first to discover that noose around your neck, so why the running? Why the fuss? You have a woman sacrificing her personhood on one of your shoulders, a man saving his existence on the other, and the thought of having them both defeats you utterly.<br /><br />If you had been the sole defeated, you may have been redeemed. But no. You ignored the truth of women surviving in the 1950's, you belittled the love of a man with far more than you to lose, and wrenched yourself out of your belovedly loathed dreamland in as bloody a manner as can be. Off you go, another quest for what you cannot bear to lose even to the undisclosed desires of your confusion and your shame, your manhood and your lust, the path your father led you and the lies with which you pave your way, off to a future of balancing over the gap.<br /><br />The worst of it is that you acted as anyone would. Better, maybe, worse, perhaps, but the reader knows the garrote of love and the lemming of its lifelines. There is no hating you without hating what they themselves commit in the name of affection and a socially acceptable relationship. Outside of that is only a sick sense of empathy and an even sicker sense of gratefulness that their personal hell is not your own.<br /><br />The rest, as we say, is history, and we are doomed to repeat it.<blockquote>
  <i>"Well then," he continued, "as though with enough time and all that fearful energy and virtue you people have, everything will be settled, solved, put in its place. And when I say everything," he added, grimly, "I mean all the serious, dreadful things, like pain and death and love, in which you Americans do not believe."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2985217983134560366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15833513602782630020">This book is so damn heartbreaking...<br/> <br/>This is the first James Baldwin book that I have ever read and... my first impression was that he was such an amazing writer! <br/><br/>Once I started reading this small book, I just couldn't stop myself and I ended up reading it in one sitting.<br/><br/>I love how the characters were so realistically developed. I would say this one is a classic for a reason. <br/><br/>The story is set in the 1950s in Paris where one character staying away from home falls for a bartender. Things get comp</span>
  <span id="freeText15833513602782630020" style="display:none">This book is so damn heartbreaking...<br /> <br />This is the first James Baldwin book that I have ever read and... my first impression was that he was such an amazing writer! <br /><br />Once I started reading this small book, I just couldn't stop myself and I ended up reading it in one sitting.<br /><br />I love how the characters were so realistically developed. I would say this one is a classic for a reason. <br /><br />The story is set in the 1950s in Paris where one character staying away from home falls for a bartender. Things get complicated as this character is caught in between his morals and beliefs, decides to marry woman ultimately. <br /><br />But the consequences of all this leading to a tragic ending and heartbreaks.<br /><br />The story deals with sexual identity and several social issues, most importantly how the gay community was looked upon those days. <br /><br />Sadly, such issues are still prevailing. And yes, for that matter I would always support the LGBTQ community 🙋<br /><br />However, I would say this is a must read. I would say the best parts are the dialogues between the woman and the main character towards the end of the book.<br /><br />So many quotable lines! This is one of those few books which made me annotate and actually underline sentences 📝<br /><br />The only parts where I didn't like were how women were described in the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15833513602782630020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_409136994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/409136994" />
    <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls"><img alt="MJ Nicholls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374341850p2/2386804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/409136994?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MJ Nicholls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MJ Nicholls" href="/user/show/2386804-mj-nicholls">MJ Nicholls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=merkins">merkins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=penguin-classics">penguin-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2386804-mj-nicholls?shelf=novels">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer409136994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer732982602026509422">Baldwin picked up where Gore Vidal left off in <i>The City & the Pillar</i>. This novel renders Vidal’s effort a tame, breezy vacation at the hotel de homo, sizzling as it does with dirty-realist conflict, torturous identity politics, and one of the whiniest lovers since Courtney Love hooked up with the entire population of Iran. One frustrating conflict—Baldwin wanted to escape the “Negro writer” ghetto, so made his characters (it would seem) white in this novel. Imagine the stink if he’d written abou</span>
  <span id="freeText732982602026509422" style="display:none">Baldwin picked up where Gore Vidal left off in <i>The City &amp; the Pillar</i>. This novel renders Vidal’s effort a tame, breezy vacation at the hotel de homo, sizzling as it does with dirty-realist conflict, torturous identity politics, and one of the whiniest lovers since Courtney Love hooked up with the entire population of Iran. One frustrating conflict—Baldwin wanted to escape the “Negro writer” ghetto, so made his characters (it would seem) white in this novel. Imagine the stink if he’d written about a black man-on-man romantic affair. In escaping his cage he might have bypassed the opportunity of the century. Still, <i>Giovanni’s Room</i> is an audacious, spectacular example of the power of literature to free the repressed, comfort the lost, and nudge the helpless toward some sort of assistance. Love this man.</span>
  <a data-text-id="732982602026509422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2507143705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2507143705" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55478778-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462205788p2/55478778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2507143705?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/55478778-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11448957-giovanni-s-room">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55478778-laura?shelf=never-to-be-forgotten">never-to-be-forgotten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55478778-laura?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55478778-laura?shelf=men">men</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2507143705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2434602376279417330">The writing is so good, no wonder everyone likes this. I have only one fault, and it's a fairly major one - the murder and guillotine were not necessary. There is so much pain and sorrow endured and regretted, through David's careless, ugly betrayal, and Giovanni's loss and subsequent dissolution that - for me and for them - it was enough. <br/><br/><i> 'You want to leave Giovanni because he makes you stink. You want to despise Giovanni because he is not afraid of the stink of love. You want to <u>kill</u> him in t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2434602376279417330" style="display:none">The writing is so good, no wonder everyone likes this. I have only one fault, and it's a fairly major one - the murder and guillotine were not necessary. There is so much pain and sorrow endured and regretted, through David's careless, ugly betrayal, and Giovanni's loss and subsequent dissolution that - for me and for them - it was enough. <br /><br /><i> 'You want to leave Giovanni because he makes you stink. You want to despise Giovanni because he is not afraid of the stink of love. You want to <u>kill</u> him in the name of all your lying little moralities. And you-you are <u>immoral</u>. You are, by far, the most immoral man I have met in all my life. Look, <u>look</u> what you have done to me. Do you think you could have done this if I did not love you? Is <u>this</u> what you should do to love?'</i><br /><br />Everything in the book, pales in contrast to that central scene when David returns to the room to collect his belongings, and Giovanni is sitting naked on the edge of the bed, willing with every fibre of his being for David to change his mind. He doesn't. <br /><br />And we hear also how much David suffers; from the beginning we know he suffers. The events of their love affair and Giovanni's subsequent actions are told in flashback, interspersed through the forward action of the novel.<br /> <br />But Baldwin is commited to a tragedy and his plot grinds ruthlessly towards murder. There is a section where David envisions how the murder must have taken place, and because he knows Giovanni's history and the anguish he suffers, it all seems very plausible, but for me, I have lost interest. On the other hand, there is a scene, in the house in the south of France, after Hella has gone. It is David's redemption, where he finally accepts his denial of love, his cruelty to Giovanni, and the mistakes he has made. I think he also realizes that he is profoundly implicated in Guillaume's murder, not by any direct action but because there were consequences to his behaviour. And of course, there is the sorrow of realizing that none of what has happened can be undone. <br /> <br />Separated from Giovanni, by his decision to be with Hella, David, imagines Giovanni's final hours, in his cell. The three executioners arrive to carry, to walk him along the corridor etc - this is David's agony. Me - all I could think was - you could have gone, you could have gone there to be with him. But Baldwin, quite correctly knows that enough is enough.<br /><br />The relationship with Hella - David is so pleased to see her when she returns from Spain, but he is not in love with her. He is simply relieved -not to have to deal with the situation of Giovanni, the loss of his job, his poverty and his DEPENDENCE on him, David - it is all just too much for David. I don't want to say this character is weak, but he is young - he was brought up in a society that stymied gay people - he was afraid. He couldn't see how it would be possible to have a life with Giovanni - no imagination. <br /><br /><i>'What kind of life can we have in this room? - this filthy little room. What kind of life can two men have together, anyway?</i><br /><br />And Hella - I had very little sympathy for her. She confesses at the end that she knew, but that she needed David to confirm his homosexuality - in some way - to at least tell her he had feelings for Giovanni, but I can only think - she knew even before she left for Spain - otherwise why else leave David to 'think things through'.<br /><br />And as Giovanni says: <i> 'You are not leaving me for a <u>woman.</u> If you were really in love with this little girl, you would not have had to be so cruel to me.'</i><br /><br />Everything ties together so well in this book. All the time Giovanni knows that David cannot commit to him. There is the scene where David is indicating to Giovanni that he will leave him one day, and Giovanni says:<br /><br />'<i>Why, you will go home and then you will find that home is not home any more. Then you will really be in trouble. As long as you stay here, you can always think: One day I will go home.' He played with my thumb and grinned. 'N'est-ce pas?'<br /><br />'Beautiful logic,' I said. 'You mean I have a home to go to as long as I don't go there?'<br />He laughed. 'Well isn't it true? You don't have a home until you leave it and then, when you have left, you never can go back.'</i><br /><br />Giovanni is so much wiser than our silly American David - a metaphor if you like - home is where the heart it. This is what Giovanni means, he knows David better than David knows himself.<br /><br />I loved the beginning of this book - the long, long scene of the first meeting - just the four central characters - David, Giovanni, Jacques and Guillaume; the drinking, the innuendo, the marvellous play of word and action, overseen by Mme. Clothilde - and finally the separation of David and Giovanni, where they can enjoy their oysters and white wine alone - and yet we have been told all that we need to know about this secretive underworld of the bars and bistros of Les Halles.<br /><br />At the beginning, just after the very first conversation between David and Giovanni there is a little scene, a sort of microcosm or foreshadowing of everything to follow - this is where I really sat up and thought - I am in the hands of a genius:<br /><br /><i> Now someone whom I had never seen before came out of the shadows towards me. It looked like a mummy or a zombie -this was the first, overwhelming impression of-of something walking after it had been put to death. . . . It carried a glass, it walked on its toes, the flat hips moved with a dead, horrifying lasciviousness. It seemed to make no sound; this was due to the roar of the bar . . . It glittered in the dim light; the thin, black hair was violent with oil, combed forward, hanging in bangs; the eyelids gleamed with mascara, the mouth raged with lipstick. The face was white and thoroughly bloodless with some kind of foundation cream; it stank of powder and a gardenia like perfume. The shirt, open coquettishly to the navel, revealed a hairless chest and a silver crucifix. . .<br />I was not sure that he was coming toward me but I could not take my eyes away...</i><br /><br />There follows an exchange between this 'ghost', and Daivd, whereby the transvestite or cross-dresser, observes that Giovanni and he have hit it off; when David refuses to acknowledge this the 'ghost' warns David:<br /><br />'<i>Il est dangereux, tu sais.</i> And for a boy like you- he is<i> very</i> dangerous.' [He asks David for a drink:] 'Oh, my poor friend, so young, so strong, so hand-some will you not buy me a drink?'<br />'<i>Va te faire foutre.</i>'<br />His face crumpled in the sorrow of infants and of very old men . . . '<i>T'aura du chagrin,</i>' he said. 'You will be very unhappy. Remember that I told you so.'<br /><br />I liked this whole scene very much - I've shortened it here. It's almost as if this 'ghost' is David, or possibly Giovanni's ghost that will haunt him. It reminded me a great deal of the witches in Macbeth who foretell what will happen to him. And of course it is also Peter refusing to acknowledge Jesus.<br /><br />And this brings me to my final, or rather my first point - I kept thinking that Baldwin, really wanted this novel to be a play - and as a play the plot would have fitted more convincingly into the traditional tragedy format. This was Baldwin's second novel, first published in 1957, when he was a young man - 33 years old. He had moved to Paris, to escape the restrictive moral values in the United States, and it is there that he met the young man, to whom this novel is dedicated - Lucien. <br /><br />I think Baldwin was ambitious for recognition when he wrote this novel; if he had been a more experienced writer with an established reputation I think he would have been confident to leave the story within the confines of love betrayed. The extra details of murder and the death sentence ratchets this disturbing and already powerful story a little beyond what the reader needs. But there again, I did not have to live as a gay, black man in the 1950s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2434602376279417330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i75PVBZrYadvOjJ8IbLucQ2ixtuvGCFsC3EJIsDndcqxmCaGrTWoz8gRhh3WR+Su2/0hE2GVrwtQD0+TDaSHUA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vEccPALhHNBitRpo9jI/8u19CXi0pfo2YP3CxBD7Wy6GYXXuub/VuMWergkBxzUtOyLusHoodFE7g4R13biptA==')})
  }

But a chance meeting by the river soon becomes an intense, exhilarating, and all-consuming affair. After their camp duties are fulfilled, the pair spend a dreamlike few weeks camping in the countryside, bonding over an illicit copy of James Baldwin’s Giovanni’s Room. Inhabiting a beautiful natural world removed from society and its constraints, Ludwik and Janusz fall deeply in love. But in their repressive communist and Catholic society, the passion they share is utterly unthinkable.\n\nOnce they return to Warsaw, the charismatic Janusz quickly rises in the political ranks of the party and is rewarded with a highly-coveted position in the ministry. Ludwik is drawn toward impulsive acts of protest, unable to ignore rising food prices and the stark economic disparity around them. Their secret love and personal and political differences slowly begin to tear them apart as both men struggle to survive in a regime on the brink of collapse.\n\nShifting from the intoxication of first love to the quiet melancholy of growing up and growing apart, Swimming in the Dark is a potent blend of romance, post-war politics, intrigue, and history. Lyrical and sensual, immersive and intense, Tomasz Jedrowski has crafted an indelible and thought-provoking literary debut that explores freedom and love in all its incarnations.<\/span>\n  <a
