Written when the speaker, Little Dog, is in his late twenties, the letter unearths a family\'s history that began before he was born — a history whose epicenter is rooted in Vietnam — and serves as a doorway into parts of his life his mother has never known, all of it leading to an unforgettable revelation. At once a witness to the fraught yet undeniable love between a single mother and her son, it is also a brutally honest exploration of race, class, and masculinity. Asking questions central to our American moment, immersed as we are in addiction, violence, and trauma, but undergirded by compassion and tenderness, On Earth We\'re Briefly Gorgeous is as much about the power of telling one\'s own story as it is about the obliterating silence of not being heard.\n\nWith stunning urgency and grace, Ocean Vuong writes of people caught between disparate worlds, and asks how we heal and rescue one another without forsaking who we are. There he meets Mitko, a charismatic young hustler, and pays him for sex. He returns to Mitko again and again over the next few months, drawn by hunger and loneliness and risk, and finds himself ensnared in a relationship in which lust leads to mutual predation, and tenderness can transform into violence. As he struggles to reconcile his longing with the anguish it creates, he’s forced to grapple with his own fraught history, the world of his southern childhood where to be queer was to be a pariah. There are unnerving similarities between his past and the foreign country he finds himself in, a country whose geography and griefs he discovers as he learns more of Mitko’s own narrative, his private history of illness, exploitation, and disease.\n\nWhat Belongs to You is a stunning debut novel of desire and its consequences. With lyric intensity and startling eroticism, Garth Greenwell has created an indelible story about the ways in which our pasts and cultures, our scars and shames can shape who we are and determine how       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin">About James Baldwin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1343346341p3/10427.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin">James Baldwin
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6122296902252223600"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i><br/><br/>James Arthur Baldwin was an American novelist, essayist, playwright, poet, and social critic.<br/><br/>James Baldwin offered a vital literary voice during the era of civil rights activism in the 1950s and '60s. He was the eldest of nine children; his stepfather was a minister. At age </span>
  <span id="freeText6122296902252223600" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i><br /><br />James Arthur Baldwin was an American novelist, essayist, playwright, poet, and social critic.<br /><br />James Baldwin offered a vital literary voice during the era of civil rights activism in the 1950s and '60s. He was the eldest of nine children; his stepfather was a minister. At age 14, Baldwin became a preacher at the small Fireside Pentecostal Church in Harlem. In the early 1940s, he transferred his faith from religion to literature. Critics, however, note the impassioned cadences of Black churches are still evident in his writing. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17143.Go_Tell_It_on_the_Mountain" title="Go Tell It on the Mountain" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Tell It on the Mountain</a>, his first novel, is a partially autobiographical account of his youth. His essay collections <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/410810.Notes_of_a_Native_Son" title="Notes of a Native Son" rel="nofollow noopener">Notes of a Native Son</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38458.Nobody_Knows_My_Name" title="Nobody Knows My Name" rel="nofollow noopener">Nobody Knows My Name</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/464260.The_Fire_Next_Time" title="The Fire Next Time" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fire Next Time</a> were influential in informing a large white audience.<br /><br />From 1948, Baldwin made his home primarily in the south of France, but often returned to the USA to lecture or teach. In 1957, he began spending half of each year in New York City. His novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a>, about a white American expatriate who must come to terms with his homosexuality, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38474.Another_Country" title="Another Country" rel="nofollow noopener">Another Country</a>, about racial and gay sexual tensions among New York intellectuals. His inclusion of gay themes resulted in a lot of savage criticism from the Black community. Eldridge Cleaver, of the Black Panthers, stated the Baldwin's writing displayed an "agonizing, total hatred of blacks." Baldwin's play, Blues for Mister Charlie, was produced in 1964. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38469.Going_to_Meet_the_Man" title="Going to Meet the Man" rel="nofollow noopener">Going to Meet the Man</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38461.Tell_Me_How_Long_the_Train_s_Been_Gone" title="Tell Me How Long the Train's Been Gone" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me How Long the Train's Been Gone</a> provided powerful descriptions of American racism. As an openly gay man, he became increasingly outspoken in condemning discrimination against lesbian and gay people.<br /><br />On November 30, 1987 Baldwin died from stomach cancer in Saint-Paul-de-Vence, France. He was buried at the Ferncliff Cemetery in Hartsdale, near New York City.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6122296902252223600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
